## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling / solid mechanics
**Analysis**: The task seeks the stress-strain-temperature relationship for a material, which is a core problem in constitutive modeling where stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic laws and on temperature through thermal softening or thermally-activated mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening, Hollomon equation)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress offset)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon) (saturation-type hardening)
- Johnson-Cook strain-temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T**c5) (combined hardening and thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook homologous form: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T) (hardening with exponential thermal softening)
- Arrhenius thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated flow stress)
- Linear thermal softening with power hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T) (power hardening times linear softening)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * epsilon**(c3 - 1))**(-1) (nonlinear elastic-plastic)
- Swift law with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(-c3 * T) (shifted power law with thermal softening)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (Sellars-Tegart / Zener-Hollomon type)
- Polynomial thermal modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic temperature-dependent modulus)
- Coupled power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Stress proportional to strain multiplied by a decreasing function of temperature: epsilon * f(T) where f is linear, exponential, or power-law decay in T
- Strain hardening saturation → Exponential approach to limit: c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)), indicating dislocation density saturation
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant plus strain-dependent term: c0 + f(epsilon), representing initial yield followed by hardening
- Multiplicative separability → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), common in constitutive models where strain hardening and thermal softening are independent factors
- Thermally activated processes → Arrhenius-type exp(c0 / T) or exp(-c0 * T) terms reflecting Boltzmann statistics of dislocation motion
- Homologous temperature scaling → Temperature appears as (T_m - T) or (1 - c0*T) reflecting distance from melting point
- Concave-up to concave-down strain response → Power law epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 captures decreasing hardening rate typical of metals
- Phase transition discontinuity → Abrupt change in stress-temperature slope may indicate structural transformation, modeled by sigmoid or tanh transitions in T

## Analysis

Let me analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression:

$$GT = 3.6246\epsilon(-0.05899(T - 367.02) + 1) + 94.205\epsilon^{0.4475}\exp\left(\frac{-55.016}{8.314T}\right) + 5.1243\epsilon\exp(-(T-367.02)^2)$$

Breaking this down:
1. **Term 1**: Linear in both T and ε: `c0*epsilon*(-c1*T + c1*c2 + c3)` = a*T*ε + b*ε (linear in T·ε and ε)
2. **Term 2**: `94.205 * ε^0.4475 * exp(-6.616/T)` — This involves ε raised to a fractional power (~0.45) multiplied by an exponential in 1/T (Arrhenius-type term)
3. **Term 3**: `5.1243 * ε * exp(-(T-367)^2)` — This is ε multiplied by a Gaussian in T

The key challenge is matching **Term 2** (Arrhenius-type: `ε^0.45 * exp(-const/T)`) and **Term 3** (Gaussian in T: `ε * exp(-(T-c)^2)`).

Looking at the candidates, they all use combinations of:
- `T*c*epsilon` (linear T·ε term) ✓ for Term 1
- `T*c` (linear T term)
- `sin(c*epsilon^(1/4) + c)` — sinusoidal in ε^(1/4), NOT equivalent to ε^0.45 * exp(-c/T)
- `sin(T*c + c)` — sinusoidal in T, NOT equivalent to exp(-(T-c)^2)
- Various polynomial terms in ε

**The fundamental problem**: None of the candidates contain:
- An **exponential decay in 1/T** (Arrhenius term `exp(-c/T)`)
- A **Gaussian in T** (`exp(-(T-c)^2)`)

The candidates use `sin()` functions to approximate nonlinear behavior, but `sin()` is periodic while `exp(-c/T)` and `exp(-(T-c)^2)` are not periodic. No choice of constants can make a sinusoidal function equal to an exponential/Gaussian for **all** values of T and ε.

Some candidates (like #34) have `T^c2` terms, but this doesn't produce `exp(-c/T)`.
Some candidates (like #25, #29, #46) have exponential terms, but:
- #25: `exp(c8*epsilon^c9)` — exponential in ε, not in 1/T
- #29: `log(c7*exp(c8*epsilon)+1)` — involves ε, not T
- #46: `exp(T*c6)` — exponential linear in T, not exp(-c/T) or exp(-(T-c)^2)

None of the candidates can reproduce both the Arrhenius term `ε^0.45 * exp(-c/T)` and the Gaussian term `ε * exp(-(T-c)^2)` simultaneously. These are fundamentally different functional forms from what's available in any candidate.

Conclusion: No match

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```

```

Let me expand the first term:
- `3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 0.05899*367.02 + 1)` = `3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 21.65 + 1)` = `3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 22.65)`
- = `-0.2139*epsilon*T + 82.10*epsilon`

So GT = `-0.2139*epsilon*T + 82.10*epsilon + 94.205*epsilon^0.4475*exp(-6.616/T) + 5.1243*epsilon*exp(-(T-367.02)^2)`

The GT has these structural components:
1. `T*epsilon` (linear in both)
2. `epsilon` (linear)
3. `epsilon^0.4475 * exp(-const/T)` - a fractional power of epsilon times Arrhenius-type term
4. `epsilon * exp(-(T-367)^2)` - epsilon times Gaussian in T

This is a complex expression with an Arrhenius term `exp(-c/T)` and a Gaussian term `exp(-(T-c)^2)`.

## Key Observations

The candidates mostly use combinations of:
- `T*epsilon`, `T` terms (linear)
- `sin(...)` functions
- `epsilon^(1/4)`, `epsilon^2`, `log(...)` terms
- Some have `exp(...)` terms

The GT contains `exp(-c/T)` (Arrhenius) and `exp(-(T-c)^2)` (Gaussian). These are fundamentally different from `sin(...)` functions. No finite combination of sinusoidal functions can exactly equal exponential/Gaussian functions across all domains.

Let me check if any candidate has the right structural basis functions:

- **Candidates with exp terms**: Candidates 18, 25, 29, 34, 46
  - Candidate 18: `c5*exp(c6*epsilon)` - exponential in epsilon, not matching `exp(-c/T)` or `exp(-(T-c)^2)`
  - Candidate 25: `c7*exp(c8*epsilon^c9)` - exponential in epsilon power, not T-dependent exponentials
  - Candidate 29: `c6*log(c7*exp(c8*epsilon) + 1)` - softplus in epsilon
  - Candidate 34: `T^c2 * c3` - power of T, not exponential
  - Candidate 46: `c5*exp(T*c6)` - exponential in T, but GT has `exp(-c/T)` and `exp(-(T-c)^2)`, neither is `exp(aT)`

None of the candidates contain `exp(-c/T)` (Arrhenius term) or `exp(-(T-c)^2)` (Gaussian in T). These are essential, linearly independent basis functions that cannot be replicated by polynomials, sinusoids, logarithms, or simple exponentials.

Since the GT fundamentally requires:
- `epsilon^0.4475 * exp(-const/T)` 
- `epsilon * exp(-(T-367)^2)`

And no candidate provides these functional forms, none can match.

Let me verify candidates with `sin` - could `sin` approximate? No, strict algebraic equivalence is required, not approximation.

Going through all 50 candidates systematically: None contain both `exp(-c/T)` and `exp(-(T-c)^2)` terms. The basis functions are fundamentally mismatched.
